<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yangtze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanjiangyuan_National_Nature_Reserve" title="Sanjiangyuan National Nature Reserve">Sanjiangyuan ("Three Rivers' Sources") National Nature Reserve</a> in Qinghai</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three_Parallel_Rivers_of_Yunnan" title="Three Parallel Rivers of Yunnan">Three Parallel Rivers of Yunnan</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yangtze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Yangtze River has a high <a href="/wiki/Species_richness" title="Species richness">species richness</a>, including many <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemics</a>. A high percentage of these are seriously threatened by human activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fish">Fish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yangtze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Acipenser_sinensis.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="723" data-file-width="2364" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Acipenser_sinensis.JPG/220px-Acipenser_sinensis.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Acipenser_sinensis.JPG/330px-Acipenser_sinensis.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Acipenser_sinensis.JPG/440px-Acipenser_sinensis.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Acipenser_sinensis.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The two <a href="/wiki/Sturgeon" title="Sturgeon">sturgeon</a> species in the Yangtze (here <a href="/wiki/Chinese_sturgeon" title="Chinese sturgeon">Chinese sturgeon</a>) are both seriously threatened.</div></div></div>
<p>As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Yangtze&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 416 fish species are known from the Yangtze <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basin</a>, including 362 that strictly are freshwater species. The remaining are also known from salt or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brackish" title="Brackish">brackish</a> waters, such as the river's <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> or the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>. This makes it one of the most species-rich rivers in Asia and by far the most species-rich in China (in comparison, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> has almost 300 fish species and the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> 160).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> 178 fish species are endemic to the Yangtze River Basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> Many are only found in some section of the river basin and especially the upper reach (above <a href="/wiki/Yichang" title="Yichang">Yichang</a>, but below the headwaters in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qinghai-Tibet_Plateau" title="Qinghai-Tibet Plateau">Qinghai-Tibet Plateau</a>) is rich with 279 species, including 147 Yangtze endemics and 97 strict endemics (found only in this part of the basin). In contrast, the headwaters, where the average altitude is above 4,500 m (14,800 ft), are only home to 14 highly specialized species, but 8 of these are endemic to the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-3"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> The largest orders in the Yangtze are <a href="/wiki/Cypriniformes" title="Cypriniformes">Cypriniformes</a> (280 species, including 150 endemics), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siluriformes" title="Siluriformes">Siluriformes</a> (40 species, including 20 endemics), <a href="/wiki/Perciformes" title="Perciformes">Perciformes</a> (50 species, including 4 endemics), <a href="/wiki/Tetraodontiformes" title="Tetraodontiformes">Tetraodontiformes</a> (12 species, including 1 endemic) and <a href="/wiki/Osmeriformes" title="Osmeriformes">Osmeriformes</a> (8 species, including 1 endemic). No other order has more than four species in the river and one endemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-4"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many Yangtze fish species have declined drastically and 65 were recognized as <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened</a> in the 2009 Chinese <a href="/wiki/Regional_Red_List" title="Regional Red List">red list</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThreatenedFish_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-ThreatenedFish-89">[89]</a></sup> Among these are three that are considered entirely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extinct" title="Extinct">extinct</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_paddlefish" title="Chinese paddlefish">Chinese paddlefish</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anabarilius_liui_liui" title="Anabarilius liui liui">Anabarilius liui liui</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Atrilinea_macrolepis" title="Atrilinea macrolepis">Atrilinea macrolepis</a></i>), two that are <a href="/wiki/Extinct_in_the_wild" title="Extinct in the wild">extinct in the wild</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Anabarilius_polylepis" title="Anabarilius polylepis">Anabarilius polylepis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Schizothorax_parvus" title="Schizothorax parvus">Schizothorax parvus</a></i>), four that are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euchiloglanis_kishinouyei" title="Euchiloglanis kishinouyei">Euchiloglanis kishinouyei</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Megalobrama_elongata" title="Megalobrama elongata">Megalobrama elongata</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Schizothorax_longibarbus" title="Schizothorax longibarbus">Schizothorax longibarbus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Leiocassis" title="Leiocassis">Leiocassis</a> longibarbus</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThreatenedFish_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-ThreatenedFish-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Animals_2020_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Animals_2020-90">[90]</a></sup> Additionally, both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_sturgeon" title="Yangtze sturgeon">Yangtze sturgeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_sturgeon" title="Chinese sturgeon">Chinese sturgeon</a> are considered critically endangered by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IUCN" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>. The survival of these two sturgeon may rely on the continued release of captive bred specimens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNAcipenserdabryanus_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNAcipenserdabryanus-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNAcipensersinensis_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNAcipensersinensis-92">[92]</a></sup> Although still listed as critically endangered rather than extinct by both the Chinese red list and IUCN, recent reviews have found that the Chinese paddlefish is extinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yirka_2020_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yirka_2020-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cheung_2020_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cheung_2020-94">[94]</a></sup> Surveys conducted between 2006 and 2008 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ichthyologists" title="Ichthyologists">ichthyologists</a> failed to catch any, but two probable specimens were recorded with <a href="/wiki/Hydroacoustics" title="Hydroacoustics">hydroacoustic</a> signals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The last definite record was an individual that was accidentally captured near Yibin in 2003 and released after having been <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_radio_telemetry" title="Wildlife radio telemetry">radio tagged</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Animals_2020_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Animals_2020-90">[90]</a></sup> The Chinese sturgeon is the largest fish in the river and among the largest freshwater fish in the world, reaching a length of 5 m (16 ft); the extinct Chinese paddlefish reputedly reached as much as 7 m (23 ft), but its maximum size is labeled with considerable uncertainty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNPsephurusgladius_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNPsephurusgladius-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="293" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg/220px-Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg/330px-Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg/440px-Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hypophthalmichthys_molitrix_Hungary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Silver_carp" title="Silver carp">silver carp</a> is native to the river, but has (like other <a href="/wiki/Asian_carp" title="Asian carp">Asian carp</a>) been spread through large parts of the world with <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The largest threats to the Yangtze native fish are <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a> and habitat loss (such as building of dams and <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>), but pollution, <a href="/wiki/Destructive_fishing_practices" title="Destructive fishing practices">destructive fishing practices</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Blast_fishing" title="Blast fishing">fishing with dynamite</a> or poison) and <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced species</a> also cause problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-5"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> About <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1020198016" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="frac" role="math"><span class="num">2</span>⁄<span class="den">3</span></span> of the total freshwater fisheries in China are in the Yangtze Basin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> but a drastic decline in size of several important species has been recorded, as highlighted by data from lakes in the river basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-6"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2015, some experts recommend a 10-year fishing moratorium to allow the remaining populations to recover,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishingMoratorium_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FishingMoratorium-100">[100]</a></sup> and in January 2020 China imposed a 10-year fishing moratorium on 332 sites along the Yangtze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Dams present another serious problem, as several species in the river perform breeding <a href="/wiki/Fish_migration" title="Fish migration">migrations</a> and most of these are non-jumpers, meaning that normal <a href="/wiki/Fish_ladder" title="Fish ladder">fish ladders</a> designed for <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> are ineffective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-7"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Gezhouba_Dam" title="Gezhouba Dam">Gezhouba Dam</a> blocked the migration of the paddlerfish and two sturgeon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNAcipenserdabryanus_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNAcipenserdabryanus-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNAcipensersinensis_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNAcipensersinensis-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IUCNPsephurusgladius_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-IUCNPsephurusgladius-97">[97]</a></sup> while also effectively splitting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_high_fin_banded_shark" title="Chinese high fin banded shark">Chinese high fin banded shark</a> population into two<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and causing the <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">extirpation</a> of the Yangtze population of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_eel" title="Japanese eel">Japanese eel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In an attempt of minimizing the effect of the dams, the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges_Dam" title="Three Gorges Dam">Three Gorges Dam</a> has released water to mimic the (pre-dam) natural flooding and trigger the breeding of carp species downstream.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatureConservancy_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatureConservancy-104">[104]</a></sup> In addition to dams already built in the Yangtze basin, several large dams are planned and these may present further problems for the native fauna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatureConservancy_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-NatureConservancy-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>While many fish species native to the Yangtze are seriously threatened, others have become important in <a href="/wiki/Fish_farming" title="Fish farming">fish farming</a> and introduced widely outside their native range. A total of 26 native fish species of the Yangtze basin are farmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishingMoratorium_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-FishingMoratorium-100">[100]</a></sup> Among the most important are four <a href="/wiki/Asian_carp" title="Asian carp">Asian carp</a>: <a href="/wiki/Grass_carp" title="Grass carp">grass carp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_carp" title="Black carp">black carp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_carp" title="Silver carp">silver carp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bighead_carp" title="Bighead carp">bighead carp</a>. Other species that support important fisheries include <a href="/wiki/Northern_snakehead" title="Northern snakehead">northern snakehead</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_perch" title="Chinese perch">Chinese perch</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Takifugu" title="Takifugu">Takifugu</a></i> pufferfish (mainly in the lowermost sections) and <a href="/wiki/Predatory_carp" title="Predatory carp">predatory carp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FishDiversity_88-8"><a href="#cite_note-FishDiversity-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animals">Other animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yangtze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChineseAlligator15.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2212" data-file-width="3100" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/ChineseAlligator15.JPG/220px-ChineseAlligator15.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/ChineseAlligator15.JPG/330px-ChineseAlligator15.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/ChineseAlligator15.JPG/440px-ChineseAlligator15.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChineseAlligator15.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Chinese_alligator" title="Chinese alligator">Chinese alligator</a> is one of the smallest <a href="/wiki/Crocodilia" title="Crocodilia">crocodilians</a>, reaching a maximum length of about 2 m (7 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Due to commercial use of the river, tourism, and pollution, the Yangtze is home to several seriously threatened species of large animals (in addition to fish): the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_finless_porpoise" title="Yangtze finless porpoise">narrow-ridged finless porpoise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baiji" title="Baiji">baiji</a> (Yangtze river dolphin), <a href="/wiki/Chinese_alligator" title="Chinese alligator">Chinese alligator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_giant_softshell_turtle" title="Yangtze giant softshell turtle">Yangtze giant softshell turtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_giant_salamander" title="Chinese giant salamander">Chinese giant salamander</a>. This is the only other place besides the United States that is native to an alligator and paddlefish species. In 2010, the Yangtze population of finless porpoise was 1000 individuals. In December 2006, the Yangtze river dolphin was declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Functionally_extinct" title="Functionally extinct">functionally extinct</a> after an extensive search of the river revealed no signs of the dolphin's inhabitance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In 2007, a large, white animal was sighted and photographed in the lower Yangtze and was tentatively presumed to be a <i>baiji</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> However, as there have been no confirmed sightings since 2004, the <i>baiji</i> is presumed to be functionally extinct at this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> "Baijis were the last surviving species of a large lineage dating back seventy million years and one of only six species of freshwater dolphins." It has been argued that the extinction of the Yangtze river dolphin was a result of the completion of the Three Gorges Dam, a project that has affected many species of animals and plant life found only in the gorges area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous species of land mammals are found in the Yangtze valley, but most of these are not directly associated with the river. Three exceptions are the semi-aquatic <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_otter" title="Eurasian otter">Eurasian otter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_deer" title="Water deer">water deer</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A8re_David%27s_deer" title="Père David's deer">Père David's deer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG/220px-2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG/330px-2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG/440px-2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_Andrias_davidianus.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The entirely aquatic <a href="/wiki/Chinese_giant_salamander" title="Chinese giant salamander">Chinese giant salamander</a> is the world's largest amphibian, reaching up to 1.8 m (5.9 ft) in length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmphWebAndrias_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmphWebAndrias-111">[111]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In addition to the very large and exceptionally rare Yangtze giant softshell turtle, several smaller turtle species are found in the Yangtze basin, its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River_Delta" title="Yangtze River Delta">delta</a> and valleys. These include the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_box_turtle" title="Chinese box turtle">Chinese box turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow-headed_box_turtle" title="Yellow-headed box turtle">yellow-headed box turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pan%27s_box_turtle" title="Pan's box turtle">Pan's box turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yunnan_box_turtle" title="Yunnan box turtle">Yunnan box turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow_pond_turtle" title="Yellow pond turtle">yellow pond turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_pond_turtle" title="Chinese pond turtle">Chinese pond turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_stripe-necked_turtle" title="Chinese stripe-necked turtle">Chinese stripe-necked turtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_softshell_turtle" title="Chinese softshell turtle">Chinese softshell turtle</a>, which all are considered threatened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>More than 160 <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibian</a> species are known from the Yangtze basin, including the world's largest, the critically endangered Chinese giant salamander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWFYangtze_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWFYangtze-113">[113]</a></sup> It has declined drastically due to hunting (it is considered a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">delicacy</a>), habitat loss and pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmphWebAndrias_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-AmphWebAndrias-111">[111]</a></sup> The polluted <a href="/wiki/Dian_Lake" title="Dian Lake">Dian Lake</a>, which is part of the upper Yangtze watershed (via <a href="/wiki/Pudu_River" title="Pudu River">Pudu River</a>), is home to several highly threatened fish, but was also home to the <a href="/wiki/Yunnan_lake_newt" title="Yunnan lake newt">Yunnan lake newt</a>. This newt has not been seen since 1979 and is considered extinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThreatenedAmphibians_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-ThreatenedAmphibians-115">[115]</a></sup> In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_fire_belly_newt" title="Chinese fire belly newt">Chinese fire belly newt</a> from the lower Yangtze basin is one of the few Chinese salamander species to remain common and it is considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_concern" title="Least concern">least concern</a> by the IUCN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThreatenedAmphibians_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-ThreatenedAmphibians-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EriocheirSinensis1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="876" data-file-width="1347" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/EriocheirSinensis1.jpg/220px-EriocheirSinensis1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/EriocheirSinensis1.jpg/330px-EriocheirSinensis1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/EriocheirSinensis1.jpg/440px-EriocheirSinensis1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EriocheirSinensis1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mitten_crab" title="Chinese mitten crab">Chinese mitten crab</a> is a commercially important species in the Yangtze,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2003_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2003-118">[118]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive</a> in other parts of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eriocheir2007_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eriocheir2007-119">[119]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The Yangtze basin contains a large number of <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_crab" title="Freshwater crab">freshwater crab</a> species, including several endemics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> A particularly rich genus in the river basin is the <a href="/wiki/Potamidae" title="Potamidae">potamid</a> <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sinopotamon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sinopotamon (page does not exist)">Sinopotamon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_mitten_crab" title="Chinese mitten crab">Chinese mitten crab</a> is catadromous (migrates between fresh and saltwater) and it has been recorded up to 1,400 km (870 mi) up the Yangtze, which is the largest river in its native range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eriocheir2007_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eriocheir2007-119">[119]</a></sup> It is a commercially important species in its native range where it is farmed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wang2003_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2003-118">[118]</a></sup> but the Chinese mitten crab has also been spread to Europe and North America where considered <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eriocheir2007_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eriocheir2007-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>The freshwater jellyfish <i><a href="/wiki/Craspedacusta_sowerbii" title="Craspedacusta sowerbii">Craspedacusta sowerbii</a></i>, now an invasive species in large parts of the world, originates from the Yangtze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOBANIS_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOBANIS-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFDW.COM"><a class="external text" href="https://www.dw.com/en/almost-all-plastic-in-the-ocean-comes-from-just-10-rivers/a-41581484" rel="nofollow">"Almost all plastic in the ocean comes from just 10 rivers – 30.11.2017"</a>. <i>Deutsche Welle</i>. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180822181401/https://www.dw.com/en/almost-all-plastic-in-the-ocean-comes-from-just-10-rivers/a-41581484" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on August 22, 2018<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 22,</span> 2018</span>. <q>about 90 percent of all the plastic that reaches the world's oceans gets flushed through just 10 rivers: The Yangtze, the Indus, Yellow River, Hai River, the Nile, the Ganges, Pearl River, Amur River, the Niger, and the Mekong (in that order).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Deutsche+Welle&amp;rft.atitle=Almost+all+plastic+in+the+ocean+comes+from+just+10+rivers+%E2%80%93+30.11.2017&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.dw.com%2Fen%2Falmost-all-plastic-in-the-ocean-comes-from-just-10-rivers%2Fa-41581484&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AYangtze"></span></span>
